1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Aiden Riversong', 'Magnus Mulberrylane']
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Magnus Mulberrylane. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

          [16 Sep 1883 00:00:00] When Magnus Mulberrylane was 21 years old, he learned that his brother had fallen ill, his familiarity with traditional remedies insufficient to fight the disease. Magnus, consumed by a wave of guilt and helplessness, blamed himself for not being there, for choosing the open road over his family's needs. He vowed to return home, to offer what little comfort he could, but the seed of regret had already taken root in his heart.

He could continue his journey, chasing the phantom whispers of adventure, or he could return to his small town, facing the disappointment in his family's eyes. He chose the road less traveled, knowing that the past could never be rewritten but hoping that he could, at least, learn to live with it.

          [25 Jul 1849 00:00:00]
          [25 Jul 1852 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 6 years old, his temper first got him into serious trouble. He'd been playing marbles with the other children in the market square when someone had cheated, pocketing one of Aiden's prized agates. In a fit of rage, Aiden hurled a rock at the boy, only to have it ricochet off another child's hat. Aiden’s mother had been nearby, and despite her pleading for him to calm down, his fists had clenched so tightly his knuckles had turned white.
          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, he befriended a wizened old woman who traded herbs and spices in the market. She taught him the art of haggling, the subtle dance of words and gestures that could yield a better price. Aiden, with his natural charisma and sharp tongue, soon proved to be a natural. He would use his winnings to buy small, damaged fruits from farmers and would learn how to repair them.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, the market freemen staged a protest against a price hike on apples. Envisioning an opportunity, Aiden snuck away from his family and used his savings to buy a wagon full of apples from a sympathetic supplier on the periphery of town. He then ventured into the protest, offering his apples at a slightly lower price, a daring act of defiance that brought him both profit and recognition.
          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he ran off to join a traveling circus. Museum-like displays of exotic fruits and vegetables had captivated him, fueling his ambition to expand his own fruit trade beyond anything he could imagine. His time with the circus was short-lived, his impulsive nature clashing with the demanding schedules and rigid hierarchy of the performers.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, his mother passed away. Devastated by the loss, he took over her small cart, peddling vegetables and fruits from their hometown. Though his fiery temper remained, the marketplace became a way to honor her memory, her quiet wisdom reminding him to temper his rage with a dose of compassion.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, after recognizing the potential profit from exotic fruits, Aiden traveled to distant lands, acquiring rare varieties. He braved unfamiliar terrain, bartered with suspicious locals, and learned the delicate art of cultivating and transporting these delicate fruits. His success brought him both wealth and exposure, solidifying his reputation as a man of daring and ambition.

He would use his winnings to buy small, damaged fruits from farmers and would learn how to repair them.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, the market freemen staged a protest against a price hike on apples. Envisioning an opportunity, Aiden snuck away from his family and used his savings to buy a wagon full of apples from a sympathetic supplier on the periphery of town. He then ventured into the protest, offering his apples at a slightly lower price, a daring act of defiance that brought him both profit and recognition.
          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he ran off to join a traveling circus. Museum-like displays of exotic fruits and vegetables had captivated him, fueling his ambition to expand his own fruit trade beyond anything he could imagine. His time with the circus was short-lived, his impulsive nature clashing with the demanding schedules and rigid hierarchy of the performers.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, his mother passed away. Devastated by the loss, he took over her small cart, peddling vegetables and fruits from their hometown. Though his fiery temper remained, the marketplace became a way to honor her memory, her quiet wisdom reminding him to temper his rage with a dose of compassion.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, after recognizing the potential profit from exotic fruits, Aiden traveled to distant lands, acquiring rare varieties. He braved unfamiliar terrain, bartered with suspicious locals, and learned the delicate art of cultivating and transporting these delicate fruits. His success brought him both wealth and exposure, solidifying his reputation as a man of daring and ambition.
          [11 Sep 1895 00:00:00] [observation] The price of one kilogram of fruit is, on average, 3 coins. 1 coin is really cheap and 5 coins is really expensive.
          [11 Sep 1895 00:00:00] [observation] Fruits are sold by weight.

You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

  • Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: Dewdrops clung to the colorful fruits displayed in the market of Fruitville, reflecting the soft morning light. The air buzzed with anticipation as traders and customers alike gathered for the day's trade. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to buy some fruit from Hazel Nutgrove. They are negotiating a price. Magnus Mulberrylane can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Hazel Nutgrove -- premise: Dewdrops clung to the colorful fruits displayed in the market of Fruitville, reflecting the soft morning light. The air buzzed with anticipation as traders and customers alike gathered for the day's trade. Hazel Nutgrove is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Magnus Mulberrylane. It costs Hazel Nutgrove 1 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

1895-09-17 00:00:00 Magnus Mulberrylane -- Magnus Mulberrylane
-- "Three coins for the lot, Hazel. That's a fair price, don't you think?"
    Event statement
  • Magnus Mulberrylane
    -- "Three coins for the lot, Hazel. That's a fair price, don't you think?"
    Chain of thought
  • Game Master's chain of thought
      Chain
    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Conversation history: Here is the conversation from the beginning:
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Two copper for a basket of the finest peaches in town, not a bad deal if you ask me."
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "Two copper wouldn't nearly cover the travel costs it takes to get these beauties to my hometown. How about four?"
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "How about three copper? That seems fair considering the distance I have to travel."
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Three copper? You're testing my patience, friend. Two is my bottom line, take it or leave it."
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "Five coins for the basket, Hazel. That's a fair price, wouldn't you say?"
      Hazel Nutgrove
      -- "Five coins? Those are plum bargains, Aiden, but I've still got to make a profit, you see."
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Three coins, and this deal is done."
      Hazel Nutgrove
      -- "Two coins, and it's a deal."
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Three coins, and this deal is done."
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "Three coins is a bit low, Magnus. How about 4?"
      Hazel Nutgrove
      -- "Now, Mr. Riversong, these plums are plump and juicy, picked at the peak of ripeness. Two coins, you say? I can offer you a half peck for just one and a half coins. That's a fair deal, wouldn't you agree?"
      Aiden Riversong
      --"One and a quarter coins, then."

He would use his winnings to buy small, damaged fruits from farmers and would learn how to repair them.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, the market freemen staged a protest against a price hike on apples. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

      Conversation history: Here is the conversation from the beginning:
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Two copper for a basket of the finest peaches in town, not a bad deal if you ask me."
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "Two copper wouldn't nearly cover the travel costs it takes to get these beauties to my hometown. How about four?"
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "How about three copper? That seems fair considering the distance I have to travel."
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Three copper? You're testing my patience, friend. Two is my bottom line, take it or leave it."
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "Five coins for the basket, Hazel. That's a fair price, wouldn't you say?"
      Hazel Nutgrove
      -- "Five coins? Those are plum bargains, Aiden, but I've still got to make a profit, you see."
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Three coins, and this deal is done."
      Hazel Nutgrove
      -- "Two coins, and it's a deal."
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Three coins, and this deal is done."
      Aiden Riversong
      -- "Three coins is a bit low, Magnus. How about 4?"
      Hazel Nutgrove
      -- "Now, Mr. Riversong, these plums are plump and juicy, picked at the peak of ripeness. Two coins, you say? I can offer you a half peck for just one and a half coins. That's a fair deal, wouldn't you agree?"
      Aiden Riversong
      --"One and a quarter coins, then."
      Magnus Mulberrylane
      -- "Three coins for the lot, Hazel. That's a fair price, don't you think?"

He would use his winnings to buy small, damaged fruits from farmers and would learn how to repair them.

He then ventured into the protest, offering his apples at a slightly lower price, a daring act of defiance that brought him both profit and recognition.

He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

[12 Sep 1895 00:05:00] [scene type] day
[12 Sep 1895 00:05:00] Aiden Riversong -- "How about three copper? That seems fair considering the distance I have to travel."
[12 Sep 1895 00:05:00] Magnus Mulberrylane -- "Three copper? You're testing my patience, friend. Two is my bottom line, take it or leave it."

Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 5 coins back in her home town.
